The `video_vendor_dmi_table` is used to identify systems where the generic ACPI video driver should handle backlight instead of acer-wmi\n3. The TravelMate 5735Z is missing from this table\n\nWhen a system is NOT in the table:\n- The DMI check at line 2207 fails\n- The brightness capability is NOT disabled\n- So acer-wmi tries to control brightness, but apparently it doesn't work well\n\nWhen the user specifies `acpi_backlight=native`:\n- The command line parameter overrides the default\n- The ACPI video driver (native) handles the brightness\n- It works with 15-16 levels\n\nSo the fix is to add TravelMate 5735Z to the `video_vendor_dmi_table` so that the system uses the generic ACPI video driver instead of acer-wmi for brightness control.\n\nLet me verify this understanding by looking at what the video_detect.c file {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01HYzW9hnj8WkDpBnmw5m1tT","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I have a clear understanding of the bug and the fix needed:1. The `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` function determines which backlight driver to use:   - First checks command line (acpi_backlight=...)   - Then checks DMI quirks from `video_detect_dmi_table` (in video_detect.c)   - Then checks if ACPI video backlight is available\n   - Then checks Win8 native backlight with RAW type\n   - Falls back to acpi-video2. The acer-wmi.c also checks a separate `video_vendor_dmi_table` and calls `acpi_video_set_dmi_backlight_type(acpi_backlight_vendor)` if a match is found3. The TravelMate 5735Z is not in the acer-wmi.c's `video_vendor_dmi_table`4. According to the bug report:   - When the system boots with default settings, it tries to use acer-wmi, which doesn't work\n   - When booted with `acpi_backlight=native`, the ACPI video driver (native) works correctly5. Now I understand the full flow:1. When acer_platform_probe is called:   - It checks if ACER_CAP_BRIGHTNESS is set in the capability   - If yes, it calls acer_backlight_init to register the acer-wmi backlight device2. The capability is set/disabled based on:   - Initially set based on what the WMI reports   - But then disabled if video_vendor_dmi_table match disables it   - And also disabled if acpi_video_get_backlight_type() != acpi_backlight_vendorFor TravelMate 5735Z:- It's not in video_vendor_dmi_table\n- So the capability is not disabled by the table match\n- But then it's checked against acpi_video_get_backlight_type()\n- If that returns something other than vendor, it's disabled\n- But then nothing controls the brightness!\n\nActually, looking more carefully at line 2210-2211:\n```cif (acpi_video_get_backlight_type() != acpi_backlight_vendor)    interface->capability &= ~ACER_CAP_BRIGHTNESS;\n```\n\nThis seems counterintuitive. Why would you disable acer brightness if it's NOT vendor? Let me look at the complete context again...\n\nOh wait, I think I finally understand! The logic is:1. If the system is in video_vendor_dmi_table:   - Call the callback which disables ACER_CAP_BRIGHTNESS   - Set DMI backlight type to vendor   - Then check if backlight type is vendor (it should be because we just set it)   - If it's vendor, don't disable (already disabled by callback)2. If NOT in the table:   - Don't set DMI backlight type   - Check if backlight type is vendor   - If it's NOT vendor, disable ACER_CAP_BRIGHTNESS (so acer-wmi doesn't control brightness)   - If it IS vendor, keep it enabled (acer-wmi will control brightness)\n\n\nThe assumption here is that acer-wmi should only manage brightness when the ACPI video driver has selected the vendor backlight type. If it hasn't, then another driver—native, video, or something else—will handle it instead. For the TravelMate 5735Z, since it's not in the table and acpi_video_get_backlight_type() likely returns acpi_backlight_video by default, the ACER_CAP_BRIGHTNESS gets disabled, preventing acer-wmi from registering its backlight device. This leaves no driver actually controlling the brightness, which is the core issue reported.\n\nThe user found that `acpi_backlight=native` resolves the problem, so the fix should force the native backlight type rather than trying to enable the vendor path. This would mean adding an entry to video_detect_dmi_table with video_detect_force_native callback. Looking at similar systems in that table, there are already precedents for using video_detect_force_vendor, video_detect_force_video, video_detect_force_native, and video_detect_force callbacks for different hardware configurations.\n\nHowever, since acer-wmi already maintains its own video_vendor_dmi_table with specific logic for determining which Acer systems should delegate to the generic
